I have some excellent .SI4 files for Fibonacci Trader SRV if anyone is interested.  
  
**UPDATED FILES POSTED AT[TRENDCHASERFX.COM](http://trendchaserfx.com)!**  
  
  
I've been working on these for quite some time and is now the only system I use and have been using for a while. Nice part is, as you FT SRV users may know, is that I don't have to watch the charts at all. I let the system run, which is 100% mechanical, and it signals my phone when a trade is called; I log in on my Blackberry and make the trade. I had thought about marketing these, but I really don't have the time or the need to make a profit on them.  
  
Even though it's mechanical 100%, it's a highly profitable system. It's a volatility based system and that's all it really requires. No news watching, no fundamental analysis...just do as your told. And obviously, don't over leverage yourself. It's a day trading method that works most efficiently on the 30-150-D FT SRV charts. I can practically guarantee that there is no more efficient system for trading the GBP/JPY than this one.  
  
~Mudd

[Forex.com](/brokers/forexcom "View FOREX.com Broker Profile") and GFT both have a platform that works with Blackberry devices. GFTs' is specifically built for BB, while Forex.coms' is a browser based app. GFT has a much nicer interface as forex.com is just boxey and ugly. I also prefer GFT as a broker due to the fact they offer more services, more platform choices, a pro platform for executive accounts, as well as over 5 sales branches. I have recieved phone calls from my account exec. every week since switching to GFT. I hadn't heard from my FXsol guy in months. I want to know that my money is safe....they give me that feeling.  
  
I'm going to type up a "READ ME" file for these .SI4's so there is no misunderstanding as to their use. I'll get these out to everyone that has requested as quickly as possible.

The TREND CHASER FX system posts a 56% success rate, which in the trading realm is an outstanding number. Especially when you consider that the wins can run for several hundreds of pips whereas loses are limited. Most traders are lucky to be 36% percent win/loss ratio even when experiencing great success.  
  
The one thing I hadn't thought of till now is that that 56% percent may be dependant on the timezone I'm in. These trades all close at EOD (End of Day). No carry overs. So, you MAY experience a slighlty lower or possibly higher percentage. Either way, this is still a great system. The best I've used personally. Hope you have as much success!!

  * Edited 7:42am  Aug 31, 2007 7:39am | Edited 7:42am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

When you recieve a signal, do as your told. DON'T ANALYSE, DON'T SECOND GUESS.  
  
Those are the only rules. Really doesn't get easier. The system is a day trading system so all trades expire at the close. For me, around 8PM EST.  
  
You must respond to the signals regardless of what time of day.   
  
You'll win....you'll lose. But you'll win much more often and more points than you ever lose.  
  
I usually back up the GBP/JPY positions with a 150 point stop loss, JUST TO BE ON THE SAFE SIDE. But I prefer to stay in till the system stops out....or calls a FLAT. I normally put on the SL when I need to leave the PC for a time.

To import the system(s), save them anywhere you like, (i.e. My Documents) and then select SYSTEMS > IMPORT on the FT SRV platform. Once imported and you have a chart open, select SYSTEMS > right click and select USE.

> So is all there to it is do what signal tells you then close it out at 8 pm est regardless of profit/loss?

> Ignored

The system will generate the FLAT at the end of the day and notify you. This primarily depends on your time zone. The system performance increased about 12% by closing positions EOD rather than carrying over. So, regardless of state, they are going to close.  
  
I was thinking about the whole time zone thing last night and figured that if someone is experiencing radical differences in performance due to their particular time zone, the easiest method would be to change the trading times to match EST - USA. So say your in Dubai which is 8 hours ahead of EST -USA, you would need to set the trading times back 8 hours.  
  
For those of you not famailiar with 24 hour military time, it's based on twelve midnight at 24:00. Past midnight is 00:01, 00:02, etc. One o' clock in the morning would be 01:00, 02:00 for two and so on. Twelve noon is 12:00 with one o' clock in the afternoon as 13:00. 14:00 for 2:00 and so on. 14:00 Sunday minus 8 hours for Dubai would need to be set as 08:00.  
  
This may overcome performance differences due to time zone. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

Couple more questions, if you would be so kind Muddbuddha.   
  
I have it all set up (only on gbp/jpy 30-150-D chart) and at 10:30 AM est I get texted "sell 1 short at 234.2200 Now SHORT 1" So I place a short at 234.22 and just hang out  
  
at 12:30 est I get text'd "Buy 1 at 233.76 Now FLAT" What does that mean? Is it referring to an old buy signal just telling me whats going on? or is that a new signal to buy now and get out of my short?  
  
4:06 EST I get text'd "Buy 1 at 233.48 Now FLAT"   
  
I am assuming that "Buy 1" is an old signal that was started before I got the platform up and I am getting texts on the status of it and that the signal to short 1 meant go Short. So I hypothetically would have 2 open orders one short and one long? And I would hold them both until 7pm EST before closing them regardless of profit/loss?  
  
I am sorry if these are remedial questions but I am trying to understand this system and I am sure some of these other fine folks might be wondering the same thing.

  * [#26](/thread/post/1570914#post1570914 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 1, 2007 6:29am  Sep 1, 2007 6:29am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

_I have it all set up (only on gbp/jpy 30-150-D chart) and at 10:30 AM est I get texted "sell 1 short at 234.2200 Now SHORT 1" So I place a short at 234.22 and just hang out_  
  
**Correct. Open a SHORT with 1 LOT**  
  
_at 12:30 est I get text'd "Buy 1 at 233.76 Now FLAT" What does that mean? Is it referring to an old buy signal just telling me whats going on? or is that a new signal to buy now and get out of my short?_  
  
**FLAT means that for whatever reason the system has declared the trade invalid. If it's prior to EOD, then the primary reason would be a retrace and close back above the trailing volatility line....or a progressive climb in the other direction. One of those two reasons. At this point, you would close your position.**  
  
4:06 EST I get text'd "Buy 1 at 233.48 Now FLAT"   
  
I am assuming that "Buy 1" is an old signal that was started before I got the platform up and I am getting texts on the status of it and that the signal to short 1 meant go Short. So I hypothetically would have 2 open orders one short and one long? And I would hold them both until 7pm EST before closing them regardless of profit/loss?  
  
**No. It called that one as the EOD, "you better be out by now" call. BUY 1 at 233.48 Not FLAT means that the trade is longer valid so buy one lot to close out the SHORT position. Sometimes it may seem like a repeat. It's just a little quirk it has. You would only get a old signal if the opening was VERY close to when you fired up the platform.**  
  
**Fibonacci Trader was originally built for stocks and options and was ported over to forex. So it doesn't have the ability to hedge a position of the same symbol.**

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

For those just starting to set up charts, if you open the charts screen and select new chart, the pair symbol, and then place 30 in the first time box and hit TAB, FT will auto in the rest of the boxes.  
  
There is a chance that FT automatically adjusts for timezone difference....not quite sure since I've only used it in EST - USA.

  * [#29](/thread/post/1570926#post1570926 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 1, 2007 6:47am  Sep 1, 2007 6:47am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

I would normally never discuss pip gains as I typically couldn't care less about how many I close out, but to serve as an example to how effective this extremely easy system is (unless it wakes you up at 2:30 AM ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f641.png?v=15.1) ), I went ahead and did the math and found I closed out 558 pips this week. That was after a 86 point stop out earlier this week.  
  
Now, to stiffle any comments as to, "What about non volatile weeks?", well you still have a better than 50% chance of a weekly gain, so this is how I approach that. I check the FF calendar a few times a week. I really don't care whether the news comes in bad or good and rarely even watch the charts around news time. What I am looking for is the chance of a volatile week. A highly voaltile whipsaw week just feeds this beast with lots and lots of $$. A not so volatile week still feeds th beast but to a lesser degree....so....up your lots. This way you compensate for the lack of volatility. On volatile weeks, lower your lots to the normal level.  
  
If I close 200 a week, I'm fine. I'm not in a race or competition with anyone. My goal is financial freedom...not bragging rights. **558 was a decent week for trading one pair on the 30 minute chart and never actually seeing the chart.**

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

1.) get a "FLAT" signal then exit  
2.) get an opposite signal then exit current position and open new position in opposite direction  
3.) exit at 7PM EST if #1 and #2 didn't happen regardless of P&L.  
  
Maybe I misunderstand your post and #2 shouldn't ever happe. Please let me know if those rules are wrong, I'm just trying to get the semantics right. I don't mean to come across as a knucklehead.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> Okay, if I got this right..like you said earlier just do what it tells you, and when it says "FLAT" exit out, or exit at 7pm EST if no "FLAT" call is given? and you shouldn't have a short and long open at the same time for any reason? I want to make sure I have this right when I demo next week![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)
> 
> Ignored

Right....except for the 7pm part. I stay in UNTIL it tells me to exit. It will FLAT at EOD unless there is a reason to prior.  
  
If you get a SHORT 1, and an hour or so later you recieve, NOW LONG 2, it's basically performing a STOP AND REVERSE where you buy 2 lots in the opposing direction to close out the ones short and enter one long. It will never have to positions at one time. But don't jump the gun on the EOD exit; let the system go. You never know what might happen. I jumped the gun about two weeks ago thinking I had milked it clean and in the last 30 minutes it drop another 150+. The system knows what it's doing.![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

I apologize, but I know nothing about MT4 scripting at all, so I can't be much help there...possibly skyline. I've been slow to get the second batch of emails out as I've been working late this week on an emergency project for the State, so posting the files here probably would be the best method.  
  
I'm suprised by the overwhemling response to the first post. Didn't quite expect this many requests. If you're expecting a highly complex system of technical formulation....this aint it. This is a trailing volatility system that thrives on the GBP/JPY; and the GBP/JPY has a long history of high volatility. If you think it's hard to trade now, you should have seen it back around 1998 when it plummented over 3000 pips like a hot iron through butter. It seems to climb, climb, climb...reach a breaking point and then fall into a lower orbit only to start its ascent again. I'm not really that interested as to why, just that it does. I don't have to know how the mountain was formed to admire its' majesty. That is the GBP/JPY in a nutshell.

Well that will take me a bit of digging. It's similar to the trailing stop, chandler stop, and volatility stop indicators you can find on Tradestation and MT...._but not quite the same. Also, FT SRV is fairly unique in it's three time frame approach to charting._ Not saying it can't be done, cause I really don't know. Just not sure how easy it would be personally.  
  
I'm not going to beat around the bush about it's value. Typically one decent trade will pay for FT SRV for a month or two. A GOOD trade will pay for FT SRV for a year! A couple of good trades and you have yourself a charting package as well as a Blackberry! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1) I have no issues with spending money to make money. Which is why I have stuck with FT and this particular system. I also have a T-Mobile line specifically dedicated to the Blackberry which I use only for trading. I believe in it _THAT MUCH_. Not saying it's easy....I hate getting woken up at 3AM from a deep sleep to open and close a trade; but at the same time it gives me a sense of excitement knowing that I may wake up to find the GBP/JPY has taken off on another 200-500 pip run. I'm not selling FT, just that I believe in its value as far as trading. I've read all the threads about the GBP/JPY which seem to be growing all the time. It's an exciting and frustrating pair to trade soley on personal discretion and analysis. I've had such good success with it on this system that I thought I would share this little secret system. I know how frustrating it can be to trade, trade, trade, and never seem to get anywhere.  
  
Also, I didn't invent this system. It's not even really a system at all. It's just an indicator that I kept playing with over and over trying different ideas until I was able to get it around 55% successful. Out of the last 51 trades, its won 30 and lost 21. Giving it a current rating of 58.82%. It's won up to 4 times in a row and lost twice in a row. It averages about 130-150 pips per win with the recent top at 430 pips and the largest loss at 138. You typically get 2-4 signals per week, maybe less if the movement is strong. You won't catch all the points possible, but with those previous posted results.....who cares?! It works well with the GBP/JPY and decently with EUR/JPY. It's terrible on the EUR/USD and better than terrible on the GBP/USD. So I stick to the top dog and live off that. No point giving hard earned $$ back to a pair that doesn't deliver as much as the GBP/JPY>

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

Well, I'm not quote sure what you mean by repaint, but if I've guessed correctly you mean kinda, "After the fact".  
  
This system triggers at the bars close. That's part of what makes it so successful. A lot of times the price will come to the volatility line, sometimes cross but not close and then move on to profit. An instant trigger would have closed out and missed the profit as price was penetrating and rebounding due to stops or anything else that may make price action bouncy. The painting of the bars is not really part of the process, just eye candy to help show position, i.e. LONG, SHORT, FLAT, at a quick glance.   
  
If that doesn't answer you question let me know....but walk me through more of what you mean. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

  * [#48](/thread/post/1571576#post1571576 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 2, 2007 9:05am  Sep 2, 2007 9:05am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

I stuck it and a screenshot on the first post of the thread.  
  
Make sure the system setting is .005 after you have applied it to the 30-150-D chart. You'll find it by right clicking the system name in the upper left corner and select EDIT. Double click the trailing volatility indicator and check the setting for .005. Default is .004, but during volatile movement it trails too closely and will get stopped out too quickly.

  * [#51](/thread/post/1571586#post1571586 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 2, 2007 9:32am  Sep 2, 2007 9:32am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

Well, the only requirement of the system is volatility. Every pair climbs and falls. That's the nature of the market. Especially in the current trend of feeding on low volatility to maximize vesting potential.   
The system doesn't do anything special other than trail that volatility for however long it can prior to the reversal. How that can be a short lived effect....I'm not really sure.  
I personally don't believe that every system fails. _I do, however, believe that every trader fails._ Seeing the state of the market and trading accordingly is part of the game. If a system that needs high volatility is failing in low volatility over a prolonged period, then it needs adjusted, not abandoned. In the case of this system, you would need to only adjust the indicator parameter down to somewhere from .002 to .004.  
  
I think you'll find the market will increase in volatility as more and more traders learn that markets are easily swayed in low volume.  
  
No, I haven't acktested it for any prolonged period. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

I'm going to help out those that may not know or have the ability to set up the SMTP portion of the FT platform.....  
  
Under the EMAIL ALERTS in the GLOBAL SETTINGS (UTILITIES), use the SMTP information from the screenshot except substitute your cell info (SMS text or cell email address).  
  
Here are the email addresses for the 6 most popular cellular phone carriers:   

  1. **T-Mobile:** _phonenumber_ @**tmomail.net**  
**Virgin Mobile:** _phonenumber_ @**vmobl.com**  
**Cingular/ATT:** _phonenumber_ @**cingularme.com or @txt.att.net**  
**Sprint:** _phonenumber_ @**messaging.sprintpcs.com**   
**Verizon:**_phonenumber_ @**vtext.com**   
**Nextel:**_phonenumber_ @**messaging.nextel.com**  
  
where _phonenumber_ = **your 10 digit phone number**

If you don't know the phone carrier for the cell phone number you are attempting to call, [you can try this universal service.](http://www.tech-recipes.com/instant_messaging_tips362.html)  
  
You need to enter the email as the username authentication ([SIGNAL@trendchaserfx.com](mailto:SIGNAL@trendchaserfx.com)) and the password.   
  
I don't want to post the password in a public forum as it would risk it being used for spam. **If you're a 1KT trader, I will send you the password.**  
  
**I will also need to limit it to less than 25-50 users to make sure the signals make it through in a timely manner.**  
  
All others will need to be vouched for by someone trustworthy. If you can figure out the SMTP by Googling your mail carriers SMTP settings, just place it in the appropriate field.

> [Quoting Mr Trend](/thread/post/1571591#post1571591 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> As you can see, if you started using this in 2005, you'd drop it after the first drawdown... well most people would. And I would put money on the fact that it doesn't backtest well before that...  
>    
>  Of course, you can see where 2007 starts...
> 
> Ignored

Have you manually gone back to analysis the trades? This would help determine why the back test would see such a drop. Trailing is trailing. The pair would have to make abrupt jig jags about every 250 pips in order to have that poor of performance. Using the .005 setting should limit losses to no more than 150 points. I checked the 2004-2005 charts and the pair was still trading within a 1000 point range which should be more than sufficient to trade successfully. It's actually been in that same pip range with the recent trades.  
  
If you get stopped out more than 2-3 times in a row or your P/L is in a steady decline, utilizing any system be it automatic or manually traded....it's time to go over things.   
  
My experience is that forex traders jump from system to system too quickly without putting any blood, sweat, and tears into it first. We often look for the perfect system that will weather any storm.   
  
When I lived in Wyoming I would change my summer treads on my car to winter treads without fail every October to prepare for the Winter...._maybe life lessons can be learned in the simplest things._  
  
Take a look at the charts manually and let me know what you think. My FT platform kicks me back to 700 bars everytime I place it at more than 29,000. So I can't help you much there.

Funny you mention....I have been playing with one on the GBP/USD that was near 89% by being in all the time. As far as this particular system, mine gained 12% by closing EOD than rolling over and getting hit with the strong move reversal that is common on the GBP/JPY. I knew that others may see differing P/L values depedning on barws in history, time zone, settings, etc....just wasn't sure to what extent.  
  
To increase the bars in memory, click the options icon (chart bars) and set the bars in memory to 29000. This should bring it out quite a ways. You may want to try 30K or more...mine resets to 700 if I do but you may have better luck. You can also change it in the global settings which will make it default for any new charts you open.  
  
I'll dig up that GBP/USD system. Some of you recieved the first Trend Chaser FX system in the .zip file....that one is a fairly safe system. Not as profittable, but safe in that it only takes trades in the direction of the major trend and is based on a longer time frame. It would sometimes hold for a couple of days. I used that one for quite some time prior to stripping it down to just the Trailing Volatility indicator. FT SRV makes it so easy to design and play around with systems since it's all graphically based that I often shot around ideas on Sundays prior to the open just to see what I can come up with.

  * [#67](/thread/post/1572015#post1572015 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 3, 2007 1:19am  Sep 3, 2007 1:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

Had a decent conversation via PM...thought I'd share.  
  
_**"Also, could you comment on the ~ weekly pip gain from your system?"**_  
  
Well, I'll help as much as possible. I typically _EXPECT_ 200 points per week, but there have been weeks where the P/L gain has exceeded 800. This week was around 580 even with a stop out. Gains come in time. The key is to be patient and not get anxious about the losses. Put realistic goals on yourself and your system. Try new things and ideas....break out of the forex dogmas that often exist concerning MA systems, Naked Trading, price action,funamentals, etc. All things have benefit to an open mind and all things hinder to a closed mind.  
  
I started enjoying the most success when I stopped reading what others thought and did and traded sound, tried and true ideas. I avoided FF for a period so I wouldn't be tempted to read the most recent posts of this weeks guru. That's when I realized that the only thing making trading hard was me and me alone.  
  
When you do succeed, be proud of your accomplishments, but make it a quiet pride. Boastfulness only breeds selfishness which in turn breeds greed and vanity. Be more like Rocky and less like Mr. T. (corny 80's reference)  
  
Approach trading as a business, not a competition. Use a profit margin for your weekly or monthly goals. If you're not meeting those goals, evaluate yourself AND your system. Indentify where you are suffering albeit your system or your own temptations. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

  * Sep 3, 2007 10:06pm  Sep 3, 2007 10:06pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

Anyone interested in trying, I got a 5% performance gain by editing the STOP options to CLOSE AT EOD and REOPEN NEXT DAY. Check both and I gained 5%.  
  
You can track the performance of the system by right clicking the system name on the chart and select RESULTS. Then choose SUMMARY>PERFORMANCE>RESULTS.  
  
If anyone else experiences that, let me know.

Okay, I know you guys are going to want to smack me.....but.....  
  
I was playing around with some settings since Mr. Trend had been talking about the 2004-2005 performance and came across this.  
  
If you add the same indicator to the system a 2nd time, but change the setting to .009 and then click USE AS TREND INDICATOR & ALL TREND INDICATORS MUST BE IN THE SAME DIRECTION.  
  
Uncheck OPEN NEXT day in the STOP options screen; keep CLOSE AT EOD; close the system screen. You should see a nice increase in performance.  
  
Check out the screens below. Try if you like, or stick with the original....it's a holiday so I had time to play around.![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

_"Does it ever tell you to close midway thru a bar, or is it a true bar close system where it has to close on the other side of the line before signalling  
the flat?"  
_  
No, it will signal at the bars close for a FLAT; and unless it's also EOD, it should signal a reversal if the price crosses back through the T.V. line.

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#100](/thread/post/1573916#post1573916 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 4, 2007 7:18am  Sep 4, 2007 7:18am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

And that is always a risk even with regulation. The fact is once a broker enters into bankruptcy hearings, your money is stuck. Every trader should take the ability of their broker to be there in 5-10 years very seriously.  
  
When you reach 200K will they allow you to pull 65K from your account all at once? Regardless of whether if it is yours or not, you'd be surprised at the excuses a lot of brokers will come up with to persuade you not to. It could be for a kidney transplant...they couldn't care less.  
  
Check their operation. How many offices...how many staff. Are they still developing their platform(s) or letting them age? Are they keeping up with technology and demand? These questions won't guarantee that they won't fold, but they can give you clues to a company that is loosing money. Does your broker shut down for several hours on U.S minor (bank) holidays (excludes christmas, easter, thanksgiving, etc.) ? Even though the U.S. is on holiday doesn't mean the whole world is. I got stopped out on a profitable position about a year ago because my broker was closed from 11-7 for the holiday observance while the rest of the world continued to trade. I couldn't close when it came time around 2PM and had to watch it go negative and stop out when they came back online at 7PM. Servers run regardless of there being anyone in the office or not. These are the kind of things to watch for and avoid as you mature in trading. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

I use IB. Comms and spread equal to around 4-5 on GBPJPY... not bad at all. They are interbank [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") and sometimes I can get 1 pip on GBPJPY... albeit for a second or two.  
  
They're entire setup and the way they operate (tight margin requirements and risk adverse ideals) is why they are the professional's choice. And why when you talk to successful traders, they trade with IB or people like MB who are known for their futures platform for YEARS.  
  
I don't understand why people go with hinky dinky brokers. It must be the infomercial thing or somethin'...go with the big guys who have been around awhile like IB, MB Trading, etc. The only retail FX broker I would even consider is [Oanda](/brokers/oanda "View OANDA Broker Profile"). 

Mr. Trend

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar9594_4.gif) Daemien](daemien)

  * | Joined May 2006  | Status: The Number of the Beast! | [395 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=9594)

Muddbuddha:  
  
It has been quite a while since I have spent any amount of time on the systems posted here. I have given yours a thorough look and backtest with Fib Trader and have posted some excellent results. I wanted to share my data with you in regards to closing out at EOD vice not closing out.  
  
I set the # of bars on the chart to 29000 (seems it won't go higher than 30000)...  
  
Date: 03/07/2005 to 03/09/2007  
  
218 Trades  
  
Results with closing at EOD: 2710 pips  
Results NOT closing at EOD: 6308 pips  
  
Clearly this is a strong argument for not closing out at EOD. Both scenarios put on 218 trades; with a 9 pip spread for GJ this = 1962 pips lost due to spread (ouch!)  
  
Thank you wholeheartedly for sharing such a simple system. I will be forward testing it shortly and will share my results here!  
  
Best in trading,  
  
D.

> Disliked
> 
> Perhaps this argument gives more weight to not closing EOD?
> 
> Ignored

Or it feeds a trader's emotional flaw of always having to be in a trade... ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
  
You have to figure out who you are in this game and always be honest with yourself. If you're a daytrader, be a daytrader. If you're a swing trader, be a swing trader. If you work on a system that has great P/L, but it's in and out of trades all day like a kamikaze, and you know that you'd be biting your nails all day, then perhaps that's not the right system for you. What **will** happen is that you won't follow the system and you'll lose, no matter how profitable it is... 

Mr. Trend

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar9594_4.gif) Daemien](daemien)

  * | Joined May 2006  | Status: The Number of the Beast! | [395 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=9594)

Just an update to my previous post:  
  
Even with closing out at EOD off, you will still be out of the market occasionally.  
  
I had an issue with the exit signals - they seemed to pop up even in the middle of some pretty strong trends. I played with it and found the following:  
  
If you turn Heiken Ashi ON, it gives you much better exits, to the tune of 9,277 pips for the same time period as I posted above.  
The largest losing trade in this scenario was only 158 pips!  
  
Performance Results for GBP/JPY 30- 150- D System Trend Chaser FX   
From 03/07/2005 21:30 to 04/09/2007 02:00   
  
HEIKEN ASHI ON  
  
Gross Profit 170.20  
Gross Loss -77.43  
Net 92.77  
Profit Factor 2.20  
  
Total Trades 195.00  
Total Winning Trades 92.00  
Total Losing Trades 103.00  
Average Points per Trade 0.48  
Percent Profitable 47.18  
  
Largest Winning Trade 9.47  
Largest Losing Trade -1.58  
Average Winning Trade 1.85  
Average Losing Trade -0.75  
Ratio Average Win/Average Loss 2.46  
Average Trade 1.27  
  
Max Consecutive Winners 5.00  
Max Consecutive Profit 14.47  
Max Consecutive Losers 7.00  
Max Consecutive Draw Down -5.96  
  
Maximum Open Interest 1.00  
Maximum Open Interest Average 1.00  
  
Again, the only change to the original is EOD close OFF & Heiken-Ashi ON. Also just to clarify I am using the last change that MuddBuddha made (with the two volatility indicators).  
  
D.

Been there, done that. Look at the opening of the heiken-ashi bar and then look at the actual open of the bar. Big difference. That's because HA bars are an average of the open. So your results would be totally flawed. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
Ahhh, the joys of creating systems. Just when you think you found that smooth equity curve, it comes back and slaps ya right in the face. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
  
I was creating a system one time, and I had HA bars up and a couple other ideas on the system, and I thought I was gonna be a millionaire in about a year. As I was going through my system while forward testing, I realized there was a big flaw somewhere... the flaw was entering off of the open of the HA bar... not even close to reality. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) I was so disappointed. But you get used to that in system development.  
  
I swear -- out of twenty ideas, two work... ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

Mr. Trend

  * Sep 4, 2007 7:53pm  Sep 4, 2007 7:53pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) Glad to see everyone is enjoying tinkering with the system(s) and expolring new ideas. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)   
  
That is the basis of being a self earning trading is the ability to recognize areas of possible improvement, try, test, and try again until you come up with a system that _YOU_ are satisfied with.   
  
FT will give you the tools to do just that without learning a scripting language and allows you to try several ideas within a short period of time.   
  
Don't hesistate to try variations of other peoples ideas. Check your backtest for sustainable profits with minimal drawdown. Save your systems and make reference notes if necessary. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

I would have assumed that the fib trader program would have used the actual price, not the averaged (heiken ashi) in the backtest - I will have to take a look at this as if it doesn't that is a major flaw in the program. With HA it's not normally the price you are interested in, just the change of colour to signify end or start of a trend - as long as the backtest positions exit with the REAL price then it should be accurate.  
  
I hope this thing isn't as buggy as MT4 with it's EA backtesting .. that thing's a piece of shite.  
  
D.  
  
  

> [Quoting Mr Trend](/thread/post/1574210#post1574210 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Been there, done that. Look at the opening of the heiken-ashi bar and then look at the actual open of the bar. Big difference. That's because HA bars are an average of the open. So your results would be totally flawed. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * Sep 5, 2007 12:51am  Sep 5, 2007 12:51am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar8946_8.gif) Mr Trend](mr*trend)

  * Joined Apr 2006 | Status: Mmmm pips. | [1,418 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=8946)

> [Quoting Daemien](/thread/post/1575426#post1575426 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I would have assumed that the fib trader program would have used the actual price, not the averaged (heiken ashi) in the backtest - I will have to take a look at this as if it doesn't that is a major flaw in the program.
> 
> Ignored

No, it's not a flaw. It's actually the **correct** way of showing Heiken-Ashi. You're just used to MT, which requires an indicator just to show those bars, which is a bastardized way of doing things.  
  
If you go look up the definition of Heiken-Ashi, you'll see that any program that **does** show it like FT does, is actually correct.  
  
MT is a good program for the cost (free) and for those who are starting out in trading, but to be quite honest, it's a piece of crap. Check out Neoticker, eSignal, Tradestation, Ensign, and FT. Those are the guns that have been around awhile and have stood the test of time. (Neo is a little new, but it rocks.) 

Mr. Trend

  * [#125](/thread/post/1575628#post1575628 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 5, 2007 1:29am  Sep 5, 2007 1:29am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar21458_4.gif) Westie](westie)

  * | Joined Oct 2006  | Status: Trader | [150 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=21458)

Here's how I get email and cell alerts for anyone that doesnt know how.  
  
First I signed up a email account with bluebottle  
then fill the fields as such,  
  
SMTP Server: mail.bluebottle.com  
Sender name: mudd signals  
Sender Email: [Whatever@bluebottle.com](mailto:Whatever@bluebottle.com)  
Recipient Name: Whatever  
Recipient Email: [Whatever@bluebottle.com](mailto:Whatever@bluebottle.com)  
cc: [10digitphonenumber@mobile.celloneusa.com](mailto:10digitphonenumber@mobile.celloneusa.com)   
  
Turn use authentication on:   
username:whatever@bluebottle.com  
password: whatever your bluebottle password is.   
  
  
This way you get a email and a cell alert, you can obviously  
have no email and just cell alert by putting the cell number in the   
recipient email field.  
  
hope that helps anyone that can't figure it out.

  * [#131](/thread/post/1575975#post1575975 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 5, 2007 4:43am  Sep 5, 2007 4:43am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

Yeah, it's practically impossible to develop one that doesn't show some type of drawdown from initial use. What I look for the most are the severity of drawdowns and a nice increasing trendline of equity. A jagged mountain range it tough to deal with. When you're on the wrong side of the mountain you feel as though your system is failing you, though you may be out of it within a day or two. A nice ascending slope is easier on the nerves overall.  
  
I saw your system, lep....what profit rating did your platform generate? Also, what JPY cross are you using? 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

  * [#146](/thread/post/1576578#post1576578 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 5, 2007 12:37pm  Sep 5, 2007 12:37pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar8946_8.gif) Mr Trend](mr*trend)

  * Joined Apr 2006 | Status: Mmmm pips. | [1,418 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=8946)

I forgot to mention to everyone creating systems. Never create a system that executed "at bar close." Because that's not real world. You always want to execute at "next bar's open", because you can get some slightly off results. It's not substantial, but when you start talking about slippage and whatnot, it can be.  
  
Unfortunately, FT doesn't do a good job of allowing you to add slippage. Tradestation, on the other hand, does do a good job as I recall...  
  
Regardless, hope that helps. 

Mr. Trend

  * Sep 5, 2007 8:19pm  Sep 5, 2007 8:19pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

> 
> Disliked
> 
> It would be be great and will save us a lot of screen watch if we could arrive at a compromise and a solutution for a profitable set up using 4 hr time frame for this method
> 
> Ignored

Well, the time frame is subjective to the method and doesn't necessarily garauntee that you have to take fewer trades. Also consider that FT has the ability to "see" three time frames at once. That being said, the Trend Chaser built on the 30-150-D typically only takes a trade once a day. If you want to hold position longer, then gradually increasing the TF can be effective. However, on volatile pairs with systems where you rely on the system to call the trade flat Vs. a set stop line, you could go extremely negative on longer time frames when events occur, like the subprime scare, that cause the market to dump suddenly. **Not saying you shouldn't use longer timeframes, just don't box yourself into a set time frame because that's what you've always used._Use what works_ and provides you the level of security that you're looking for personally.**  
  
This is acutally my first system that EVER traded on the 30 minute charts. I typically prefer the hourly. In this case, the performance was substantially higher on the 30 and still took trades about once a day.  
  
I like to stay somewhat active in the market so trading once a day is no big deal for me, considering it's typically through my Blackberry; and the TF applied to the system normally limits the stop outs to no more than 80-90 points. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

Mudd,  
Several posts ago, you and Mr. Trend were discussing the different results that were seen when enabling/disabling the EOD feature and I recall you sticking with EOD enabled due to a higher winning percentage. I compared the results ( 2 volatility indicators) from 3/26/06-9/5/2007 and I saw that the winning percentage was higher (~6%) however the results with EOD enabled netted ~2000 more pips. I made the same comparison using the original system as well and results with EOD enabled netted over 2000 more pips as well. I am curious to know if you see what I see, and if so, could you give your thoughts on why you'd choose the greater winning percentage over the greater net pip gain, if this is the case? Also, I am forward testing the lastest update (2 volatility indicators) using 1 mini lot, are you currently using this system or the original? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#156](/thread/post/1577821#post1577821 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 6, 2007 12:32am  Sep 6, 2007 12:32am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

I'm actually trading it with EOD off at the moment. While the win percentage was higher, the NON-EOD setting did enable it to bank more pips per trade which offsets the lower win percentage a majority of the time.  
  
It becomes a risk when you're in the big trades when they hit, but allowing your equity to get chewed little by little on the small losses. You have to find a balance where the scales are tipped slightly in your favor all the time. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

  * Sep 6, 2007 1:30am  Sep 6, 2007 1:30am

Well, for those of you who don't feel compelled to catch the entire movement, but are satisfied with tidbits at a higher lot level....  
  
Try using the Trend Chaser on the 30-150-D EUR/JPY with no EOD and a profit target of **75** pips. You can also use the same system on the GBP/USD with a profit target of **55** pips. This increases the win percentage and makes for an _extremely pretty_ equity curve. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

I think it also comes down to who you are as a trader. For example, I know I need to be in a trade most of the time, so I trade nothing but stop and reverse systems... If I closed a trade at EOD and it ended up going another 100 pips in my favor, I'd go nuts.  
  
There isn't anything wrong with that, per se. As long as you are following your plan. You just need to know who you are. 

Mr. Trend

  * Sep 6, 2007 2:33am  Sep 6, 2007 2:33am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar8946_8.gif) Mr Trend](mr*trend)

  * Joined Apr 2006 | Status: Mmmm pips. | [1,418 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=8946)

The best you can do is 29000 bars in memory, and I have the server collect data back to 1/1/2005. If you're serious about creating a system and have one where you think it's definitely worth working on some more, then I would suggest buying tick data. If you have an account with [Oanda](/brokers/oanda "View OANDA Broker Profile"), you can get free tick data. And OandA is known for their data before they started as a big broker, so... 

Mr. Trend

> [Quoting MuddBuddha](/thread/post/1577938#post1577938 "View Quoted Post")

> Disliked
> 
> Well, for those of you who don't feel compelled to catch the entire movement, but are satisfied with tidbits at a higher lot level....  
>    
>  Try using the Trend Chaser on the 30-150-D EUR/JPY with no EOD and a profit target of **75** pips. You can also use the same system on the GBP/USD with a profit target of **55** pips. This increases the win percentage and makes for an _extremely pretty_ equity curve.
>

  * [#165](/thread/post/1578116#post1578116 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 6, 2007 3:14am  Sep 6, 2007 3:14am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

No stop loss. The trailing volatility line will call a flat if the price returns back across or a stop and reverse if the price penetrates both lines in the same time frame. With the .004/.005 settings, the loss level is within a controlled range.   
  
I typically also put on a trading platform stop loss that is higher than where the system would call a flat just in the event of a major move due to unforseen events. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

Posted are the .SI4 files for the EUR/JPY, EUR/USD, and GBP/USD.  
  
This is a short take profit method with a higher win percentage. The TP's are 75 for EUR/JPY, 55 for GBP/USD, and 40 for EUR/USD.  
  
Trading all of them will practically guarantees a daily trade(s).  
  
Let me know what you think.![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60e.png?v=15.1)

Thanks, bapxzy! I appreciate it.  
  
Lep, the differing settings act as a type of deadband between long and short to filter noise that maybe strong enough to close one position but not have the ability to carry through with the next position. If you had ever tried the Dolly sytem on MT4, it acted in the same manner with a deadband around the open that had to be crossed by price to the topside or bottomside prior to intitaiting a trade. It's also a popular method for daily chart traders who will place entries above and below the previous days close. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

Well, since this was a rather low volatility week, I added two extra pairs to make up for it. I'm only shooting for 25 on EUR/USD positions (83%) and 55 on GBP/USD. 65 on EUR/JPY. This keeps the success rate higher than usual and gets me into some positions, though each one is relatively small.  
  
The GBP/JPY is "No limit, EOD", but of course it can snap at anytime and shoot 200-300.  
  
I've got several differing screens under the "Page" screen that I load and unload depending on how the week is progressing.  
  
A basic two pair screen with the serpents tail, a three pair screen which lacks the GBP/JPY, and the four pair screen when the market is REALLY rangey and quiet.   
  
The EUR/USD is really non-volatile for the most part, so I ALWAYS use a limit on it, otherwise it will chew you up little by little. Go small...around 25-30 at the most. You won't get many, but you will get some.  
  
Sorry about the confusion on the screens....but I will name it whatever seems to make sense to me the most at the time. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

Okay, here is a system for eur/usd I made up. Its based on 2 MACDs on a 5m time frame. It is always in, no EOD.  
  
Its made 200 pips per week for 3 weeks. I wish I could back test this further. 73% winning trades, with profit factor greater than 4. Anyway, here it is if anyone wants to improve it, let me know via this thread or PM.

Mr. Trend

  * | Joined May 2006  | Status: The Number of the Beast! | [395 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=9594)

Hey everyone!  
  
I just wanted to post a quick update on these methods...  
  
One thing to look out for when testing is the number of trades made during the particular time period. 8000+ pips over 2 years sounds great until you factor in that it took 800 trades to do so @ 9pips spread per trade. A lot of results seem to be skewed due to this.  
  
I am still unsure if I will be subscribing - I am finding that the program is hanging at times and does not send out the appropriate open or close position. There also seems to be some 'slippage' from when the signal goes out to when you receive it and manage to enter the trade (probably my txt message provider). On top of this I am frequently inside RF emission free zones due to my work requirements. I have missed a few signals so far because of these issues...  
  
And btw, the majority of the systems posted fail miserably in the first half of 2004 - nice gains are pretty well 100% given back in the span of a few months. It has been clear sailing since, however so all is not lost. Just shows how fickle this beast can be!  
  
Take care all & good luck with your trades!

  * [#194](/thread/post/1594078#post1594078 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 14, 2007 11:42pm  Sep 14, 2007 11:42pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar35717_6.gif) JoshDance](joshdance)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: Trader | [606 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35717)

Just a thought--when we take human discretion out of the picture (good discretion I mean) and rigidly follow a system, aren't all systems subject to fail over the long run? Unless a system can adapt to new conditions and markets, which is ultimately really only reasonably possible through a human's intervention, isn't even the best system bound to fail?  
  
If a system produces great results for 20 years, but blows up on year 21, what's the point? I suppose a solution would be to say that the max drawdown be at a certain percentage, say, 40% or something--when it reaches that drawdown, shut it down. But then it would be time to switch systems, and the system-hopper would be at it again. Ultimately, isn't trader psychology the key, regardless of the system? So why this endless search for systems that have backtested well over the last 5 years or something? That really says little about how well it may perform this coming year, right?  
  
Don't mean to get off the topic or anything, but this subject always seems to come up. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#196](/thread/post/1594136#post1594136 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 15, 2007 12:33am  Sep 15, 2007 12:33am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

And you made some good points.  
  
While I take back testing into consideration when creating/modifying a system, the results will ultimately be dependant on the trader. I'm not a personal fan of auto trading; I had my shot with it and it worked ok.  
  
I follow the system fairly strictly, but there have been occasion where I've been stopped out repeatedly in the same direction and have backed off taking those directional trades because I realized I was trading against strong momentum.   
  
My biggest problem with the periods where the system seems to tank is why?  
  
The system is based on a simple principle of trailing price action. If there is an extended period where it continually fails, figure out why and adjust.  
  
Do the trailing volatility indicators need tightened due to low volatile market conditions? Should I switch to a higher volatile pair? Should I use a conservative limit of 65-100 pips? Is the volatility SOOO high that good trades are turning bad because I'm staying in too long?  
  
These are discisions that the PC can't make. These need to be made by the trader and the system adjusted.....not scraped....just tweaked to match current conditions.  
  
This is why I mentioned tracking a margin percentage every month or quarter and maintaining as best as possible that margin. If you can comfortably perform 3% at $XXX,XXX.000 then hold yourself to that and track your performance....obviously adjusting as your balance grows to reflect the true margin. When I speak of margin, I'm referring to the business definition whereas a person who sells a job or contract meets a margin requirement laid out by his/her corporation that must be meet. In most companies that would be 35%.  
  
If you see that your performance is dropping month after month, spend some time figuring out why. Is it me? Is it the market?; which would mean it's really me! or is the system needing tightened and adjusted to trade the current volatility levels? 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

  * [#197](/thread/post/1594300#post1594300 "Post Permalink")

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar35717_6.gif) JoshDance](joshdance)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: Trader | [606 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35717)

Seems like a good plan MuddBuddha.  
  
As I'm sure you know, there are umpteen methods out there for calculating (in other words, not eyeballing and discretionary human opinion) market conditions and volatility. One is by Kaufman, who calculates what he calls an Adaptable Moving Average and uses an "efficiency ratio" to determine market conditions. Might be something to look into if anyone's interested in that kind of thing. But after looking at it, while it may be helpful to some, I found it's basically just another number to me. I'm not good with indicators in general, they all start to look garbled to me after a while :-) I use multiple moving averages, both guppy, hull, and another here by linuxtroll that he calls the rainbow. They are great for me to visually see what's going on with the trend and it gives fantastic entry opportunities and is great for scalping (exit is based on quick profit as a multiple of amount risked). Sorry for the rambling, and thanks for your reply!

> [Quoting JoshDance](/thread/post/1594078#post1594078 "View Quoted Post")

> Disliked

> Just a thought--when we take human discretion out of the picture (good discretion I mean) and rigidly follow a system, aren't all systems subject to fail over the long run? Unless a system can adapt to new conditions and markets, which is ultimately really only reasonably possible through a human's intervention, isn't even the best system bound to fail?  
>    
>  If a system produces great results for 20 years, but blows up on year 21, what's the point? I suppose a solution would be to say that the max drawdown be at a certain percentage, say, 40% or something--when it reaches that drawdown, shut it down. >

> Ignored

It keeps coming up and that's why if you're a systems developer, you have to continously create new systems.  
  
Trading, and the development of systems, needs to be something you enjoy. I don't think enough people get that.  
  
One thing you fail to realize is that systems don't just all of a sudden fail. If you've developed a system and you've been trading it successfully the last two years, and then in year three you make 20% less, and then in year four, you make 20% less than that, then you need to sit up and take notice that the market may be changing for your respective edge.  
  
Hence, why you always need to be looking and working on new systems.  
  
If you don't like that, then you don't develop systems. You trade discretionary with certain rules.  
  
Discretion is fine. It's just another way to trade. 

Mr. Trend

  * [#205](/thread/post/1597609#post1597609 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 18, 2007 5:02am  Sep 18, 2007 5:02am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar42849_4.gif) lepiricus](lepiricus)

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Don't steal me pot 'O pips | [547 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=42849)

Here is the first one I came up with. Its simply the QQE crossover on a 60 min chart and a 30,10,10 stochastic as a filter. I set TP at a hard 150 and stop is 100 pip trailing. The remarkable thing about this on is its equity curve, max drawdown of 62 pips. I wish I could backtest it further. But here it is.

  * Sep 19, 2007 6:11am  Sep 19, 2007 6:11am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar8946_8.gif) Mr Trend](mr*trend)

  * Joined Apr 2006 | Status: Mmmm pips. | [1,418 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=8946)

> [Quoting lepiricus](/thread/post/1600065#post1600065 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> If a guy were to just take the long signals from it, even if the trade is negative some pips he could bank some mean swap.
> 
> Ignored

But in hindsight, that's the case with GBPJPY. You don't know what the future will bring, and you don't know if we're gonna have another two year tear up.  
  
Tread lightly with systems on GBPJPY. Make sure that the theory behind your system makes sense... that's the key. Anyone could've bought on dips last two years and would've made bank.  
  
The question is how would this system do during range markets? If it breaks even, then you might be ok -- here's why:  
  
You can't realistically expect most systems to perform well during all types of markets -- hence why systems degrade over a set amount of time. But what you can look for when creating systems is those periods of time where your system is not necessarily supposed to perform that well but yet DD is kept to a minimum. THAT is a good system, because if a pair (like GBPJPY) has a tendancy to trend over a lengthy period of time, the odds are that you will be safe with a trend-based system. So if you do get rangy periods, and it breaks even or is slightly positive, then you are in good shape. You can at least stop using it after a certain period of "breakevenness", and turn to your range-based strategy.  
  
On the other hand, if you are backtesting a system that is based on trending theory, and see that it performs horribly in a ranging market on an otherwise trending pair, then you should be careful, because you never know when that market is going to change and you will lose a chunk of capital.  
  
Hope that makes sense. 

Mr. Trend

  * [#215](/thread/post/1600551#post1600551 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 19, 2007 12:02pm  Sep 19, 2007 12:02pm 

  * [ fxtradera](fxtradera)

  * | Joined Jan 2006  | Status: Trader | [63 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=5435)

I managed to download and display data back to Jan-3, 2005 for the system on 4hr bars. Attached display (if it works) should show profitability and equity curve.  
  
The equity curve was flat until Nov-2005 before it took off. Why? I'm not sure - I just did this, so haven't had a chance to review. Worth looking at further to understand.  
  
To retrieve this much history, I set the max bars at 29,700 (click the FT logo at top left of chart) and I downloaded history from the FT Server - right click on chart, choose FT server, then update 240min bars. Less charts you have and open for the GJ, the quicker the download will work.  
  
The MFE and MAE stats under the Show Detail option in Results offer some valuable data. MFE illustrates that on a number of trades, a lot of pips were left on the table before the system triggered the reversal. You can export these stats into an Excel sheet and then write formulas to identify effective profit targets and also perhaps stop loss values.   
  
There's a lot more when you scratch under the covers.   
  
Hope that helps.

  * Sep 21, 2007 3:52am  Sep 21, 2007 3:52am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

One thing that I neglected to mention while using FT4 SRV is that you can trend your systems performance and use discretion as to when to trade the system and when not to.  
  
Here are the P/L charts of the GBP/JPY and EUR/JPY versions of Trend Chaser.  
  
Notice where I've enclosed the 10 and 20 MA crossovers....the P/L charts display when the system is in a period of drawdown. Most of the time the actual cross of the 10/20 is about the same time as the drawdown period is over; but a change in slope can indicate that market conditions have changed and you should use more discretion.   
  
I'm posting this in response to a couple of comments I recieved about the stop outs at the beginning of the week. I switched over to the EUR/JPY and traded my way through it after a couple of GBP/JPY stop outs.  
  
Keep an eye on your P/L reports. While they may not represent your actual P/L experience, they are a useful tool to determine market conditions and adjust your trading strategy appropriately.

That's always something you could explore.  
  
The account link is on FT's website.

> [Quoting matrixebiz](/thread/post/1690798#post1690798 "View Quoted Post")

> Disliked
> 
> What brokers are the best then for this type of platform? and how much is the minimum $ I can open an account with? Just getting used to MT4 ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

> Ignored

Hi matrixebiz,  
  
Sounds like you are new to trading. Welcome to this mad world. You are in for a wild ride!  
  
Mudd, mentioned a broker earlier in this thread. I forget which, so start from post #1 and skim through til you find it.  
  
Minimum money to open an account. That is easy. ZERO!!!  
  
Since you do appear to be new to trading, the worst thing you can do is open a live account with real money. You should demo trade exclusively until you are fully confident in the system you are using, and are also consistently profitable.  
  
When, and only when, you've met the above conditions should you open a live account. When you do, run away as fast as you can from opening a mini account with only $300. You would have to start your trading with 10000/300 = 33.33:1 true leverage. That amount of leverage is insane, even for an experienced trader. If you don't know the difference between true leverage and broker leverage, then take a look at my sticky in the beginners forum.  
  
When you do open a live account, the minimum amount you should deposit in my opinion is twice the size of the lot you'll be trading. For example, if you open a micro account (highly recommended), each microlot is valued at 1000 units, so you should deposit $2000. If you open a mini account (NOT recommended if your account is under $40,000) then your minimum deposit should be $20,000.  
  
Dial 

sxaxlxvxaxtxixoxnxbxyxgxrxaxcxexdxoxtxoxrxgx

> I've read that you moved to FXCM to receive the SRV charts for free, but they don't have mobile platform, so, how do you manage your trades now? what do you do if you are in a BBQ or in the street and a signal email arrives? are you carrying a lap all the time?

> Ignored

Well, the one pro-active thing I do is monitor the charts regularly so I'm aware of when a potential trade may be coming up. During the week I'm typically around a PC somewhere, but still may get pulled into meetings and what not. That may cause me to miss a trade from time to time. Most of the 30 minute systems have limits, so I'm okay there. If I feel it may get stopped out, I'll put a hard stop where the volatility line is and let it run. Normally I only use an "emergency" stop of 150 pips from entry so if something happens and I cannot access a PC due to weather, car accident, etc., I won't go bankrupt.  
  
It would be great if FXCM would come out with a mobile platform as I felt a bit more secure with it, even though I didn't use it all that often. They do intend on supporting MT-4 in early 2008 which has a mobile platform, so I would need to switch phones.

MuddBuddha keep an eye on EFX's Remote Trader software which should have a full release this Jan./08. Its free like Metatrader and has been developed as a Metatrader replacement to trade through EFX. Not having your broker deal against you is huge. The software will be accessible from any Internet Explorer enabled brower plus have full mobile accessiblilty.  
  
Their full indicator programming language won't be released until a few months later and it remains to be seen if it could duplicate your "trailing volatility" indicators but this is the software of the future!!!!...as far as free one's go.

Yeah, it was a hell of an improvement. I'd been trying for a while to figure out the right TP level to smooth that pair out.   
  
The other night I was studying the performance report and saw that the back test said AVERAGE WINNING TRADE = 1.26 (126). So, I decided to try the average win with no stop loss and no RSI.   
  
Badda bing, badda boom, now you've got yourself a smoother curve....go figure.  
  
Only took me a year. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f644.png?v=15.1)

  * Jan 8, 2008 9:09pm  Jan 8, 2008 9:09pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

I realized last night that I had not included a README file for the .SI4 files. Hopefully there weren't too many people confused by the trade alerts?  
  
Systems overview:  
  
*NOTE: The first numeric of the time period line is the proper time frame to trade the system on. 30-150-D would be the 30 minute chart. 5-25-75 would be the 5 minute chart. D-W-M would be the DAILY chart. Deviation from the designed timeframe may result in negative equity P/L.  
  
1.G Systems: Trade (2) lots at position open with a trailing stop loss and set limit that both shed (1) lot when triggered. Upon shedding, the remaining lot position stays active until stopped out and reversed by the Trailing Volatility indicator, or runs to profit and is called flat at the appropriate limit level. The 1.G systems, which currently is all pairs except GBP/USD and EUR/USD Ichimoku Standard, incorporate the use of the RSI/Volatility indicators to filter trades.  
  
1.F Systems: GBP/USD ONLY. Trade (1) lot at a set limit and no stop loss. The trade is called FLAT when price penetrates and closes below or above the opposing Trailing Volatility indicator. This system does not utilize the RSI as a filter.  
  
Ichimoku Standard – EUR/USD: Trades on the DAILY chart. Rules are based strictly on the Ichimoku crossover method of the Tenkan line and Kijun line. The RSI is used a an entry filter. Trades are called FLAT when the lines cross back the opposing direction.  
  
Hopefully this clears up any confusion. I apologize for not including the README. Got a little distracted by the playoffs. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

giraia br,  
  
Right click on the screen and select, "THIS SYMBOL" > "EDIT SYMBOL PARAMETERS".  
  
For TRADING TIMES make sure SATURDAY is unchecked. End the week at FRIDAY @ 19:00 GMT and start the week on SUNDAY @ 08:00 GMT. Make sure your pip size is set to .01 and the decimal is 2.  
  
Let's see if that helps. Also, take a screenshot where the dates are visible.   
  
Let's try that and see what happens. Did you have this issue with the 1.F version>?

> Ignored

Okay, well, the heart of the system is the Trailing Volatility indicator. It works much like the Chandlier Stop and Danton Stop. It trails price at a value which represents it's offset to price. As price moves away, the TV indicator moves with it and sets it's position at the close. I could tell you the TV period for this system is .04 for one and .06 for the other. Once price has penetrated the TV line and closed, the TV line swings the other way to represent the new FLAT line.  
  
If the TV indicator can be coded properly, the rest will probably be a piece of cake. The RSI acts as a trend filter; but let's see if anyone can mimick the TV indicator first and then we'll start on the next part.  
  
Quote from other site:  
  
_"Simply, if the trend is considered up, then the trend of prices are composed of upwaves and the downwaves are countertrend movements. Downward trends are the opposite, seen as downwaves with countertrend upwaves. Using several tools and functions, we can design a quantifiable approach to defining these waves. My favorite is the volatility indicator, which is a formula that measures the market volatility by plotting a smoothed average of the true range. The true range indicator originates from the work of J. Welles Wilder Jr. from his New Concepts in Technical Trading Systems. The definition of the true range is defined as the largest of the following:_

  1. _The difference between today's high and today's low_
  2. _The difference between today's high and yesterday's close, or_
  3. _The difference between today's low and yesterday's close._

_The calculation uses a 21-period weighted average of the true range, giving higher weight to the true range of the most recent bar. The final value is then multiplied by 3._  
  
_The volatility indicator is used as a stop-and-reverse method. Let's say the market has been rising, then the volatility indicator is calculated each day and subtracted from the highest close during the rising market. The highest close is always used, even if there has been a series of lower closes since the highest close. If the market closes below the volatility indicator, then for the next day, the current reading of the volatility indicator is added to the lowest close. This step is followed each day until the market closes above the trailing volatility indicator. We now have a definition of the trend. An upward trend exists as long as the volatility indicator is below the market and a downtrend is in force if the volatility indicator is above the market."_  
  
And from another site:  
  
_"__VOLATILITY INDICATOR  
  
Editor,  
  
The September 1998 article “Trading The Trend” by Andrew Abraham, in which he presented a volatility indicator, doesn’t provide the information necessary for the educated layman who is interested in technical analysis. In my opinion, it should have provided more detail on some areas.  
  
I understand the calculation of a 21- period weighted average of the true range, but why is the final value multiplied by 3? Is the volatility indicator in a rising market calculated by subtracting the 21-period weighted average of the true range from the highest close in the same 21-period?  
  
Then when the market closes below the volatility indicator, is the volatility indicator calculated by adding the next day’s value of the 21-period weighted average of the true range to the lowest close in the 21 periods? I hope you can clarify this for me.  
  
TONY RAMSELAAR, via E-mail  
  
Weert, The Netherlands  
  
The volatility indicator discussed by Abraham in the article was originally introduced by J. Welles Wilder in New Concepts In Technical Trading, published by Trend Research in 1978, available from the Delta Society (336 698- 0500). Wilder explains that the constant used in the volatility system can range from 2.80 to 3.10 and was found by testing. The volatility indicator is a trailing stop-and-reverse approach. The volatility indicator is the average true range multiplied by the constant and subtracted from the highest close for long positions. Thus, if you are long, you should go short if the market closes below the volatility indicator. While you are short, the volatility indicator is added to the lowest close, and you go long if the market closes above the volatility indicator.  
  
I hope this helps to fill in the gaps for you.—Editor"_  
  
Please let me know as soon as you can if any of you are successful or need to ask questions. I'd be thrilled to have an EA for this on MT4! 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

This indi (TrendEnvelopes_v3)for MT4 you can find at TSD very soon.

> [Quoting freed14](/thread/post/1805518#post1805518 "View Quoted Post")

> Mudd do you think we could have a full summary of what is what. I seem to be confused by which system to use and which one is on MT4 now. If I can help let me know.

> Ignored

Okay, the .SI4's are only for the Fibonacci Trader SRV charting package.  
  
There are seven available on the website:  
  
30-150-D EUR/JPY TrendChaserFX 1.F/1.G  
30-150-D GBP/JPY TrendChaserFX 1.F/1.G  
30-150-D GBP/USD TrendChaserFX 1.F  
5-25-275 EUR/JPY 5 Minute Quicktrade 1.G  
D-W-M EUR/USD Ichimoku Standard 1.G  
  
We're got a batch of MT4 indicators on the website that now mimick the FT SRV version (1.F) fairly well, and will soon have an EA. The MT4 indicators are in a .zip file posted prior to the .SI4 files on the website. The MT4 indicators only show entry and reversal into a FLAT or opposing position. They don't show limits. These will need to be entered manually. They were E/J = 65, G/J = 75, G/U = 65 for the 30 minute systems (1.F versions).  
  
I've been runing them side by side and the entrys are identical for the most part.

> Quick question Mudda, from your experience is backtesting on Fibonacci Trader relatively reliable?

> Ignored

Well, if we're not talking tick charts, then yes, I believe so. All of the systems I've created on FT all enter based on the close which I always observed as the most reliable.  
  
Now the P/L results differ slightly from real life as there is no accounting for spread and other delaying factors in opening the trade. The data feed for FT is through [FXCM](/brokers/fxcm "View FXCM Broker Profile") and I have noticed in several cases where the trade has reached limit on FT, but my trading platform, also FXCM, didn't trigger the limit. The prices should be identical and the limit should be the limit, so I have no explanation for it right now.

  * Jan 23, 2008 7:14am  Jan 23, 2008 7:14am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

MT4 Indicator Usage:  
  
When price crosses and closes above or below the StepMA line the indicator will signal a trade by displaying the bar as either blue for LONG, or red for SHORT.   
  
Once in the trade the bar color remains the same until price starts to retrace at which time the bar color will lighten. You can either stay in and watch for reversal or close out and wait for an opposing trade or re-enter if the bar color darkens again.  
  
If price retraces back inside the Trend Bars, price will go FLAT (white), indicating no trade is available. Typically for a LONG, the RSI should be above 50 and below 50 for a SHORT.  
  
I prefer this system on the 5 minute, 30 minute, and daily charts. I feel those provide the right trend channels to profit on a regular basis. Some pairs have more "pattern persistance" than others. JPY crosses are known for this as are most GBP pairs. The CAD, however, can abruptly change direction and doesn't seem suited for this type of system.

So I take it everyone is using mostly the MT4 version. Still a great version, but lacks the notification of the FT SRV version. Unless you're trading full time, I'd stay with the MT4 though.  
  
The site thing was a pain. I'm used to getting a lot of hits from the US and Russia (don't know why, but they seem to like me in Russia?), but then started getting hits from Bulgaria on the order of 2500 a day. A little peeking into the file changes and I noticed that they were attempting to hack the blog and change the php code. Dang nine year olds have nothing better to do with their time??!!!   
  
Anyway, the site is blog free, so it should be fine. Eventually, I swear, I will have the chat room back in operation. I know alot of people miss the chat room here at FF.

Hello, MuddBuddha. actually it's quite easy to use MT4 to send you notifications, including phone calls. I've incorporated this function into one of my EAs, which I've attached here. you can either copy the appropriate function and paste it to your own EA, or send me your EA and I'll make the relevant changes for you.  
  
to make the phone calls work you need to have either a phone line connected directly to your PC thorugh an analogue modem, or have skype installed.  
  
let me know if you have any problem with this.

I still like the stepchoppy bars on mt4.  
  
Its nice even to scalp with in the direction of the trend.  
  
On one minute going from red to white bars for buys and from blue to white bars for sells.  
  
But there has to be good movement in the trend for this to work and I just look at yen crosses for this scalp.

  * May 14, 2008 9:30pm  May 14, 2008 9:30pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

Here's a small variation of the TrendChaserFX template on the 15 minute chart. It has the "trend guard" concept that I had on the .SI4 files for FT SRV.  
  
Basically, the trend guard indicates the intermediate trend direction via two higher deviation lines (envelopes), while the shorter deviation indicates entry points; the most proffitable and safest obviously being in the direction of the intermediate trend.  
  
Again, it relies on the use of the Ravi, or your choice of secondary confirmation indicators. You can grab the Ravi from TimeFreedoms post up above.
