  * [#353](/thread/post/2157676#post2157676 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 11, 2008 7:12am  Aug 11, 2008 7:12am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

_"Apart from the Ravi FX Fisher, I don't recognise the other indicator(s); is one TrendEnvelopes?"  
  
_Yes, it's the TrendEnvelopes indicator. _  
  
"If you could list the indicators and preferred settings for the daily TF that would be great."  
  
_I'm using just the TrendEnvelopes and the RAVI. The deviation for the DAILY, I've set at .04.  
  
_"Are you entering purely on RaviFx or a combination of both indicators? And how are you calculating your stop"_  
  
I wait for a signal from the TrendEnvelopes and verify the signal with RAVI. RAVI should be on the south side for a TE SHORT and vice versa. My STOP is a reversal of the TE.  
  
You can take multiple positions rather than holding one position for an extended period by closing your position on a reversal and cross of the RAVI and then placing a entry order about 50 pips above/below the current price going in the direction of the TE>  
  
Fairly straightforward.  
  
Let me know if that didn't make too much sense.

  * [#355](/thread/post/2158876#post2158876 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 11, 2008 9:24pm  Aug 11, 2008 9:24pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

Yes. You can see from this chart that I have the "USE ALERT" value set to 1 to signal an alarm window whenever price closes past the TE line going in either direction.   
  
The RAVI should already be going in the direction of the trade and on the side of the trade. If not, then I don't take it. That filters out the chops and spikes.....most of the time.  
  
"do you find this way more profitable than the first variation?"  
  
Well, profitability is relative to market conditions. There are times when the 30 minute or 5 minute variations are just kicking ass and pulling it in and then the pair will go through a transition and you'll loss one after another. The 5 seemed more profittable than the 30 if you adjusted to trading during the peak hours and didn't get crazy stupid. But you also need the time to sit in front of the PC and watch consistently. T  
  
The daily charts have been doing really well and I've been enjoying them. You can see three good shorts on the GBP/JPY aroundl ate July, early November, and then a brief one in mid February. The current up swing looks like a dead bounce and hopefully we will see a return to the downside as the RAVI is already there.

The TP is subjective. I typically close on the RAVI bottoming out and then place re-entry orders about 50 pips going in the same direction.   
  
I've posted the AUD/USD showing entries and which ones lined up with the RAVI and which ones didn't. A couple could have been good trades anyway, but the pair had become vary choppy. It is what it is.  
  
The circles are trades, the squares are bad areas.

Attachments: .SI4 for GBP/JPY & EUR/JPY

Tags: .SI4 for GBP/JPY & EUR/JPY

#  [](/thread/44790-si4-for-gbpjpy-eurjpy).SI4 for GBP/JPY & EUR/JPY 

  * 

  * [#361](/thread/post/2161732#post2161732 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 13, 2008 4:22am  Aug 13, 2008 4:22am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

No, the re-entry order is always in the direction of the TrendEnvelopes as they set the overall trend direction. The RAVI is just a tool to help determine entry and exit support.  
  
For the AUD chart above, my exit from the previous short was closed at .9125 and the re-entry occurred at .9075. I had a previous GBP close at 1.9632 and then re-open on a continuation of the SHORT at 1.9975 during an up spike to where we're sitting right now at 1.8961; so a little over 1,000 pips and holding.  
  
The point being, the trades are always in the direction of the TE. The RAVI is just a tool to aid your decision to open or close a position. When the RAVI spikes up and the TE is SHORT, I wait till the RAVI re-crosses the median and then consider going SHORT again if I don't see any evidence of other like currencies going against my trade. It also helps a little to know some patterns indicating continuations and reversals. It won't fool proof the system, but it does help out. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

  * [#370](/thread/post/2179526#post2179526 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 22, 2008 8:46pm  Aug 22, 2008 8:46pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar2564_32.gif) MuddBuddha](muddbuddha)

  * Joined May 2005 | Status: Trader | [945 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2564)

Not sure what you mean by updated, but all the indicators for the MT4 and FT SRV versions are on the website.   
  
They are also scattered here and there throughout this thread, so they can be accessed through that little paper clippy thing in the top corner.  
  
All the positions other than the AUD and NZD have re-triggered as of this morning.  
  
Not an overally exciting system to trade; down right boring for the most part. I only check it twice a day for a few minutes.   
  
The system is a straightforward trend chasing system. The only discretion or analysis needed is for exiting and re-entry strategies. Those can be fine tuned to your flavor. I use very simple methods for exiting and re-entry and they seem to work fine. **I may miss a few pips here or there or give up more than I needed to, but I'm not chained to the PC all day and still managed to pull in 1300 points in the last 30 days.**  
  
The key to not going bankrupt when you loose is to use small lots and not overleverage yourself. I know it's tempting to use larger lots and pull in the $$, but all things in their own time. Perfect your skill at exiting and entry and the $$ will eventually start coming in in larger amounts. I risk a mere fraction of my total balance and never break a sweat even if I'm 200-300 in the hole. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

Here are the templates for my current set-up.  
  
I use Deviation04_TCFX.tpl for the EUR/USD and GBP/JPY.  
  
I use Deviation05_TCFX.tpl for the GBP/USD, NZD/USD, AUD/USD, and EUR/JPY.  
  
**Please note: THERE IS NO EA FOR THIS SYSTEM. THERE WILL NOT BE AN EA FOR THIS SYSTEM. IT'S A DAILY SYSTEM THAT REQUIRES VERY LITTLE INTERFACE TIME FROM THE TRADER. IF YOU CANNOT SPEND 30 MINUTES A DAY MANAGING YOUR INVESTMENTS AND POSITIONS, YOU SHOULD BE BUYING LOTTERY TICKETS.

> [Quoting shiva](/thread/post/2204160#post2204160 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hey MudB ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) Do you trade the method exclusively on daily charts? Given that the signals arent very frequent - the interval between two signals can even be weeks.  
>    
>  What is your opinion of using this on 1h or 4h charts?
> 
> Ignored

I started using it on the 30(results on website) and have dabbled with it on the 5 and 15. I haven't really ever cared for it on the hourly or 4 hour, but it can probably be done without too much effort.  
  
Using it on the daily has required very little interaction on my part and it seems that the less I pay attention to what the market is doing throughout the day, the better my trading results are overall.   
  
Keep in mind that the signals from the TrendEnvelopes indicator are merely intermediate trend direction indications. I typically hop in and out of positions several times a week per pair; but always in the direction of the TrendEnvelopes indicator. 

Capital Preservation is key to long term wealth accumulation

> 
> Disliked
> 
> I started using it on the 30(results on website) and have dabbled with it on the 5 and 15. I haven't really ever cared for it on the hourly or 4 hour, but it can probably be done without too much effort.  
>    
>  Using it on the daily has required very little interaction on my part and it seems that the less I pay attention to what the market is doing throughout the day, the better my trading results are overall.   
>    
>  Keep in mind that the signals from the TrendEnvelopes indicator are merely intermediate trend direction indications. I typically hop in and out of positions several times a week per pair; but always in the direction of the TrendEnvelopes indicator.
